<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en"><i>The Lord of the Rings</i> (film series)</h1>			<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
				<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>				<div id="contentSub"></div>
				<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>				<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>
				<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>
				<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">This article is about the film series released between 2001 and 2003. For other films based on <a href="/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings" title="The Lord of the Rings">The Lord of the Rings</a>, see <a href="/wiki/Middle-earth_in_film" title="Middle-earth in film">Middle-earth in film</a>.</div>
<p class="mw-empty-elt">

</p>
<table class="infobox vevent" style="width:22em;font-size:90%;"><tbody><tr><th colspan="2" class="summary" style="text-align:center;font-size:125%;font-weight:bold;font-size:110%;font-style:italic;">The Lord of the Rings</th></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<a href="/wiki/File:Ringstrilogyposter.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Ringstrilogyposter.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/87/Ringstrilogyposter.jpg/220px-Ringstrilogyposter.jpg" width="220" height="146" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/87/Ringstrilogyposter.jpg/330px-Ringstrilogyposter.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/8/87/Ringstrilogyposter.jpg 2x" data-file-width="387" data-file-height="257" /></a><div style="font-size:95%;padding:0.35em 0.35em 0.25em;line-height:1.25em;">The poster for the series is a <a href="/wiki/Photomontage" title="Photomontage">montage</a> that features a range of characters and scenes from all three films</div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="white-space:nowrap;padding-right:0.65em;">Directed by</th><td>
<a href="/wiki/Peter_Jackson" title="Peter Jackson">Peter Jackson</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="white-space:nowrap;padding-right:0.65em;">Based on</th><td>
<i><a href="/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings" title="The Lord of the Rings">The Lord of the Rings</a></i><br />by <a href="/wiki/J._R._R._Tolkien" title="J. R. R. Tolkien">J. R. R. Tolkien</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="white-space:nowrap;padding-right:0.65em;">Starring</th><td>
<a href="#Cast"><i>See list below</i></a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="white-space:nowrap;padding-right:0.65em;"><div style="padding:0.1em 0;line-height:1.2em;">Production<br />company </div></th><td>
<div style="vertical-align:middle;"><div class="plainlist"><ul><li><a href="/wiki/WingNut_Films" title="WingNut Films">WingNut Films</a></li><li><a href="/wiki/Saul_Zaentz" title="Saul Zaentz">The Saul Zaentz Company</a></li></ul></div></div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="white-space:nowrap;padding-right:0.65em;">Distributed by</th><td>
<a href="/wiki/New_Line_Cinema" title="New Line Cinema">New Line Cinema</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="white-space:nowrap;padding-right:0.65em;"><div style="padding:0.1em 0;line-height:1.2em;white-space:normal;">Running time</div></th><td>

New Zealand<br />United States</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="white-space:nowrap;padding-right:0.65em;">Language</th><td>
English</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="white-space:nowrap;padding-right:0.65em;">Budget</th><td>
$281,000,000<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="white-space:nowrap;padding-right:0.65em;">Box office</th><td>
$2,917,506,956</td></tr></tbody></table> 
<p><i><b>The Lord of the Rings</b></i> is a <a href="/wiki/Film_series" title="Film series">film series</a> consisting of three <a href="/wiki/Fantasy" title="Fantasy">fantasy</a> <a href="/wiki/Adventure_film" title="Adventure film">adventure films</a> directed by <a href="/wiki/Peter_Jackson" title="Peter Jackson">Peter Jackson</a>. They are based on the novel <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings" title="The Lord of the Rings">The Lord of the Rings</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/J._R._R._Tolkien" title="J. R. R. Tolkien">J. R. R. Tolkien</a>. The films are subtitled <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings:_The_Fellowship_of_the_Ring" title="The Lord of the Rings: The Fellowship of the Ring">The Fellowship of the Ring</a></i> (2001), <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings:_The_Two_Towers" title="The Lord of the Rings: The Two Towers">The Two Towers</a></i> (2002) and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings:_The_Return_of_the_King" title="The Lord of the Rings: The Return of the King">The Return of the King</a></i> (2003). They are a New Zealand-American venture produced by <a href="/wiki/WingNut_Films" title="WingNut Films">WingNut Films</a> and <a href="/wiki/Saul_Zaentz" title="Saul Zaentz">The Saul Zaentz Company</a> and distributed by <a href="/wiki/New_Line_Cinema" title="New Line Cinema">New Line Cinema</a>.
</p><p>The trilogy was one of the biggest and most ambitious film projects ever undertaken. It had a budget of $281 to $330 million depending on the source.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> All three films were shot over eight years simultaneously and entirely in Jackson's native <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> One in every 160 New Zealanders was part of the production.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>  Each film in the series also had special extended editions released on DVD a year after their respective theatrical releases. While the films follow the book's general storyline, they do omit some of the novel's plot elements and include some additions to and deviations from the source material.
</p><p>Set in the fictional world of <a href="/wiki/Middle-earth" title="Middle-earth">Middle-earth</a>, the films follow the <a href="/wiki/Hobbit" title="Hobbit">hobbit</a> <a href="/wiki/Frodo_Baggins" title="Frodo Baggins">Frodo Baggins</a> (<a href="/wiki/Elijah_Wood" title="Elijah Wood">Elijah Wood</a>) as he and the <a href="/wiki/The_Fellowship_of_the_Ring_(characters)" class="mw-redirect" title="The Fellowship of the Ring (characters)">Fellowship</a> embark on a quest to destroy the <a href="/wiki/One_Ring" title="One Ring">One Ring</a>, and thus ensure the destruction of its maker, the Dark Lord <a href="/wiki/Sauron" title="Sauron">Sauron</a>. The Fellowship eventually splits up and Frodo continues the quest together with his loyal companion <a href="/wiki/Samwise_Gamgee" title="Samwise Gamgee">Sam</a> (<a href="/wiki/Sean_Astin" title="Sean Astin">Sean Astin</a>) and the treacherous <a href="/wiki/Gollum" title="Gollum">Gollum</a> (<a href="/wiki/Andy_Serkis" title="Andy Serkis">Andy Serkis</a>). Meanwhile, <a href="/wiki/Aragorn" title="Aragorn">Aragorn</a> (<a href="/wiki/Viggo_Mortensen" title="Viggo Mortensen">Viggo Mortensen</a>), heir in exile to the throne of <a href="/wiki/Gondor" title="Gondor">Gondor</a>, <a href="/wiki/Legolas" title="Legolas">Legolas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gimli_(Middle-earth)" title="Gimli (Middle-earth)">Gimli</a>, <a href="/wiki/Meriadoc_Brandybuck" title="Meriadoc Brandybuck">Merry</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Peregrin_Took" title="Peregrin Took">Pippin</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Wizard_(Middle-earth)" title="Wizard (Middle-earth)">wizard</a> <a href="/wiki/Gandalf" title="Gandalf">Gandalf</a> (<a href="/wiki/Ian_McKellen" title="Ian McKellen">Ian McKellen</a>) unite to rally the <a href="/wiki/Middle-earth_peoples#Free_peoples" title="Middle-earth peoples">Free Peoples of Middle-earth</a> in the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Ring" title="War of the Ring">War of the Ring</a>.
</p><p>The series was received with overwhelming praise and was a major financial success, with the films collectively being <a href="/wiki/List_of_highest-grossing_franchises_and_film_series" class="mw-redirect" title="List of highest-grossing franchises and film series">among the highest-grossing film series</a> of all time. The films were critically acclaimed and <a href="/wiki/List_of_accolades_received_by_The_Lord_of_the_Rings_film_series" title="List of accolades received by The Lord of the Rings film series">heavily awarded</a>, winning 17 out of 30 total <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Academy Award">Academy Award</a> nominations. The final film in the series, <i>The Return of the King</i>, won all 11 of its Academy Award nominations including Best Picture, which also tied it with <i><a href="/wiki/Ben-Hur_(1959_film)" title="Ben-Hur (1959 film)">Ben-Hur</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Titanic_(1997_film)" title="Titanic (1997 film)">Titanic</a></i> for most Academy Awards received for a film. The series received wide praise for its innovative special and visual effects.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Development">Development</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Lord_of_the_Rings_(film_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Development">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Director Peter Jackson first came into contact with <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings" title="The Lord of the Rings">The Lord of the Rings</a></i> when he saw <a href="/wiki/Ralph_Bakshi" title="Ralph Bakshi">Ralph Bakshi</a>'s 1978 animated film <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings_(1978_film)" title="The Lord of the Rings (1978 film)">The Lord of the Rings</a></i>. Jackson "enjoyed the film and wanted to know more."<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> Afterwards, he read a tie-in edition of the book<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> during a twelve-hour train journey from <a href="/wiki/Wellington" title="Wellington">Wellington</a> to <a href="/wiki/Auckland" title="Auckland">Auckland</a> when he was seventeen.<sup id="cite_ref-Sibley-11_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sibley-11-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1995, Jackson was finishing <i><a href="/wiki/The_Frighteners" title="The Frighteners">The Frighteners</a></i> and considered <i>The Lord of the Rings</i> as a new project, wondering "why nobody else seemed to be doing anything about it".<sup id="cite_ref-Sibley-11_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sibley-11-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> With the new developments in <a href="/wiki/Computer-generated_imagery" title="Computer-generated imagery">computer-generated imagery</a> following <i><a href="/wiki/Jurassic_Park_(film)" title="Jurassic Park (film)">Jurassic Park</a></i>, Jackson set about planning a fantasy film that would be relatively serious and feel real. By October, he and his partner <a href="/wiki/Fran_Walsh" title="Fran Walsh">Fran Walsh</a> teamed up with <a href="/wiki/Miramax_Films" class="mw-redirect" title="Miramax Films">Miramax Films</a> boss <a href="/wiki/Harvey_Weinstein" title="Harvey Weinstein">Harvey Weinstein</a> to negotiate with <a href="/wiki/Saul_Zaentz" title="Saul Zaentz">Saul Zaentz</a> who had held the <a href="/wiki/Film_rights" title="Film rights">rights</a> to the book since the early 1970s, pitching an adaptation of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Hobbit" title="The Hobbit">The Hobbit</a></i> and two films based on <i>The Lord of the Rings</i>. Negotiations then stalled when <a href="/wiki/Universal_Studios" class="mw-redirect" title="Universal Studios">Universal Studios</a> offered Jackson a <a href="/wiki/Remake" title="Remake">remake</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/King_Kong_(1933_film)" title="King Kong (1933 film)">King Kong</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-cheat_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cheat-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> Weinstein was furious, and further problems arose when it turned out Zaentz did not have distribution rights to <i>The Hobbit</i>; <a href="/wiki/United_Artists" title="United Artists">United Artists</a>, which was in the market, did. By April 1996, the rights question was still not resolved.<sup id="cite_ref-cheat_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cheat-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Jackson decided to move ahead with <i>King Kong</i> before filming <i>The Lord of the Rings</i>, prompting Universal to enter a deal with Miramax to receive foreign earnings from <i>The Lord of the Rings</i> while Miramax received foreign earnings from <i>King Kong</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-cheat_11-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cheat-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> It was also revealed that Jackson originally wanted to finish <i>King Kong</i> before <i>The Lord of the Rings</i> began. But due to location problems, he decided to start with <i>The Lord of the Rings</i> franchise instead.
</p><p>When Universal cancelled <i><a href="/wiki/King_Kong_(2005_film)" title="King Kong (2005 film)">King Kong</a></i> in 1997,<sup id="cite_ref-Timeline_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Timeline-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> Jackson and Walsh immediately received support from Weinstein and began a six-week <a href="/wiki/Chain_of_title" title="Chain of title">process of sorting out the rights</a>. Jackson and Walsh asked Costa Botes to write a <a href="/wiki/Abridgement" title="Abridgement">synopsis</a> of the book and they began to re-read the book. Two to three months later, they had written their <a href="/wiki/Film_treatment" title="Film treatment">treatment</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-quest_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-quest-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> The first film would have dealt with what would become <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings:_The_Fellowship_of_the_Ring" title="The Lord of the Rings: The Fellowship of the Ring">The Fellowship of the Ring</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings:_The_Two_Towers" title="The Lord of the Rings: The Two Towers">The Two Towers</a></i>, and the beginning of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings:_The_Return_of_the_King" title="The Lord of the Rings: The Return of the King">The Return of the King</a></i>, ending with <a href="/wiki/Saruman" title="Saruman">Saruman</a>'s death, and <a href="/wiki/Gandalf" title="Gandalf">Gandalf</a> and <a href="/wiki/Peregrin_Took" title="Peregrin Took">Pippin</a> going to <a href="/wiki/Minas_Tirith" title="Minas Tirith">Minas Tirith</a>. In this treatment, <a href="/wiki/Gwaihir" class="mw-redirect" title="Gwaihir">Gwaihir</a> and Gandalf visit <a href="/wiki/Edoras" class="mw-redirect" title="Edoras">Edoras</a> after escaping Saruman, Gollum attacks Frodo when the Fellowship is still united, and <a href="/wiki/Farmer_Maggot" title="Farmer Maggot">Farmer Maggot</a>, <a href="/wiki/Glorfindel" title="Glorfindel">Glorfindel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Radagast_(Middle-earth)" class="mw-redirect" title="Radagast (Middle-earth)">Radagast</a>, <a href="/wiki/Elladan_and_Elrohir" title="Elladan and Elrohir">Elladan and Elrohir</a> are present. Bilbo attends the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Elrond" class="mw-redirect" title="Council of Elrond">Council of Elrond</a>, Sam looks into <a href="/wiki/Galadriel" title="Galadriel">Galadriel</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Mirror_of_Galadriel" class="mw-redirect" title="Mirror of Galadriel">mirror</a>, Saruman is redeemed before he dies and the <a href="/wiki/Nazg%C3%BBl" title="Nazgûl">Nazgûl</a> just make it into <a href="/wiki/Mount_Doom" title="Mount Doom">Mount Doom</a> before they fall.<sup id="cite_ref-quest_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-quest-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> They presented their treatment to Harvey and <a href="/wiki/Bob_Weinstein" title="Bob Weinstein">Bob Weinstein</a>, the latter of whom they focused on impressing with their screenwriting as he had not read the book. They agreed upon two films and a total budget of $75&#160;million.<sup id="cite_ref-quest_13-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-quest-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>During mid-1997,<sup id="cite_ref-FOTR_SEE_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOTR_SEE-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> Jackson and Walsh began writing with <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Sinclair" title="Stephen Sinclair">Stephen Sinclair</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-quest_13-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-quest-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> Sinclair's partner, <a href="/wiki/Philippa_Boyens" title="Philippa Boyens">Philippa Boyens</a>, was a major fan of the book and joined the writing team after reading their treatment.<sup id="cite_ref-FOTR_SEE_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOTR_SEE-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> It took 13–14 months to write the two film scripts,<sup id="cite_ref-FOTR_SEE_15-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOTR_SEE-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> which were 147 and 144 pages respectively. Sinclair left the project due to theatrical obligations. Amongst their revisions, Sam is caught eavesdropping and forced to go along with Frodo, as occurs in the original novel. In the final treatment Sam, Merry, and Pippin infer the existence of One Ring and voluntarily go along after confronting Frodo about it.  Gandalf's account of his time at <a href="/wiki/Orthanc" class="mw-redirect" title="Orthanc">Orthanc</a> was pulled out of flashback and <a href="/wiki/Lothl%C3%B3rien" title="Lothlórien">Lothlórien</a> was cut, with Galadriel doing what she does in the story at Rivendell. <a href="/wiki/Denethor" title="Denethor">Denethor</a> attends the Council with his son. Other changes included having <a href="/wiki/Arwen" title="Arwen">Arwen</a> rescue Frodo, and the action sequence involving the cave <a href="/wiki/Troll_(Middle-earth)" title="Troll (Middle-earth)">troll</a>. The writers also considered having Arwen absorb Éowyn's role entirely by having her kill the <a href="/wiki/Witch-king" class="mw-redirect" title="Witch-king">Witch-king</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-quest_13-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-quest-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Trouble struck when <a href="/wiki/Marty_Katz" title="Marty Katz">Marty Katz</a> was sent to New Zealand. Spending four months there, he told Miramax that the films were more likely to cost $150&#160;million, and with Miramax unable to finance this, and with $15&#160;million already spent, they decided to merge the two films into one. On 17 June 1998, Bob Weinstein presented a treatment of a single two-hour film version of the book. He suggested cutting <a href="/wiki/Bree_(Middle-earth)" title="Bree (Middle-earth)">Bree</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Helm%27s_Deep" class="mw-redirect" title="Battle of Helm&#39;s Deep">Battle of Helm's Deep</a>, "losing or using" <a href="/wiki/Saruman" title="Saruman">Saruman</a>, merging <a href="/wiki/Rohan_(Middle-earth)" title="Rohan (Middle-earth)">Rohan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gondor" title="Gondor">Gondor</a> with <a href="/wiki/%C3%89owyn" title="Éowyn">Éowyn</a> as <a href="/wiki/Boromir" title="Boromir">Boromir</a>'s sister, shortening <a href="/wiki/Rivendell" title="Rivendell">Rivendell</a> and <a href="/wiki/Moria_(Middle-earth)" title="Moria (Middle-earth)">Moria</a> as well as having <a href="/wiki/Ent" title="Ent">Ents</a> prevent the <a href="/wiki/Uruk-hai" title="Uruk-hai">Uruk-hai</a> from kidnapping Merry and Pippin.<sup id="cite_ref-quest_13-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-quest-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> Upset by the idea of "cutting out half the good stuff"<sup id="cite_ref-FOTR_SEE_15-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOTR_SEE-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> Jackson balked, and Miramax declared that any script or work completed by <a href="/wiki/Weta_Workshop" title="Weta Workshop">Weta Workshop</a> was theirs.<sup id="cite_ref-quest_13-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-quest-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> Jackson went around Hollywood for four weeks,<sup id="cite_ref-FOTR_SEE_15-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOTR_SEE-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> showing a thirty-five-minute video of their work, before meeting with <a href="/wiki/New_Line_Cinema" title="New Line Cinema">New Line Cinema</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Mark_Ordesky" title="Mark Ordesky">Mark Ordesky</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> At New Line Cinema, <a href="/wiki/Robert_Shaye" title="Robert Shaye">Robert Shaye</a> viewed the video, and then asked why they were making two films when the book was published as three volumes (this was later corrected: New Line only made this choice out of economical reasons);<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> he wanted to make a film trilogy. Now Jackson, Walsh, and Boyens had to write three new scripts.<sup id="cite_ref-FOTR_SEE_15-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOTR_SEE-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The expansion to three films allowed much more creative freedom, although Jackson, Walsh, and Boyens had to restructure their script accordingly. The three films do not correspond exactly to the trilogy's three volumes, but rather represent a three-part <a href="/wiki/Film_adaptation" title="Film adaptation">adaptation</a>. Jackson takes a more <a href="/wiki/Chronology" title="Chronology">chronological</a> approach to the story than did Tolkien. Frodo's quest is the main focus, and Aragorn is the main sub-plot,<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> and many sequences (such as <a href="/wiki/Tom_Bombadil" title="Tom Bombadil">Tom Bombadil</a>) that do not contribute directly to those two plots were left out. Much effort was put into creating satisfactory conclusions and making sure <a href="/wiki/Exposition_(literary_technique)" class="mw-redirect" title="Exposition (literary technique)">exposition</a> did not bog down the pacing. Amongst new sequences, there are also expansions on elements Tolkien kept ambiguous, such as the <a href="/wiki/Battle" title="Battle">battles</a> and the creatures. During <a href="/wiki/Filmmaking#Production" title="Filmmaking">shooting</a>, the screenplays continued to evolve, in part due to contributions from cast members looking to further explore their characters.<sup id="cite_ref-FOTR_SEE_15-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOTR_SEE-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> Most notable amongst these rewrites was the character <a href="/wiki/Arwen" title="Arwen">Arwen</a>, who was originally planned as a warrior princess, but reverted to her book counterpart, who remains physically inactive in the story (though she sends moral and military support).<sup id="cite_ref-TTT_SEE_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TTT_SEE-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>To develop fight and sword choreography for the series, the filmmakers employed Hollywood sword-master <a href="/wiki/Bob_Anderson_(fencer)" title="Bob Anderson (fencer)">Bob Anderson</a>. Anderson worked directly with the talent including <a href="/wiki/Viggo_Mortensen" title="Viggo Mortensen">Viggo Mortensen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Karl_Urban" title="Karl Urban">Karl Urban</a> to develop the film's many sword fights and stunts.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> Bob Anderson's role in <i>The Lord of the Rings</i> series was highlighted in the film <i><a href="/wiki/Reclaiming_the_Blade" title="Reclaiming the Blade">Reclaiming the Blade</a></i>. This documentary on sword martial arts also featured <a href="/wiki/Weta_Workshop" title="Weta Workshop">Weta Workshop</a> and <a href="/wiki/Richard_Taylor_(filmmaker)" title="Richard Taylor (filmmaker)">Richard Taylor</a>, <i>The Lord of the Rings</i> illustrator John Howe and actors <a href="/wiki/Viggo_Mortensen" title="Viggo Mortensen">Viggo Mortensen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Karl_Urban" title="Karl Urban">Karl Urban</a>. All discussed their roles and work on the series as related to the sword.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Production_design">Production design</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Lord_of_the_Rings_(film_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Production design">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Alan_Lee_2005.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Alan_Lee_2005.JPG/170px-Alan_Lee_2005.JPG" width="170" height="261" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Alan_Lee_2005.JPG/255px-Alan_Lee_2005.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Alan_Lee_2005.JPG/340px-Alan_Lee_2005.JPG 2x" data-file-width="577" data-file-height="885" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Alan_Lee_2005.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Alan Lee at Worldcon 2005 in Glasgow, August 2005.</div></div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Production_design_of_The_Lord_of_the_Rings_film_series" title="Production design of The Lord of the Rings film series">Production design of The Lord of the Rings film series</a></div>
<p>Jackson began <a href="/wiki/Storyboarding" class="mw-redirect" title="Storyboarding">storyboarding</a> the series with <a href="/wiki/Christian_Rivers" title="Christian Rivers">Christian Rivers</a> in August 1997 and assigned his crew to begin designing Middle-earth at the same time.<sup id="cite_ref-TTT_Art_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TTT_Art-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> Jackson hired long-time collaborator <a href="/wiki/Richard_Taylor_(filmmaker)" title="Richard Taylor (filmmaker)">Richard Taylor</a> to lead <a href="/wiki/Weta_Workshop" title="Weta Workshop">Weta Workshop</a> on five major design elements: armour, weapons, prosthetics/make-up, creatures, and miniatures. In November 1997,<sup id="cite_ref-FOTR_SEE_15-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOTR_SEE-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> famed Tolkien illustrators <a href="/wiki/Alan_Lee_(illustrator)" title="Alan Lee (illustrator)">Alan Lee</a> and <a href="/wiki/John_Howe_(illustrator)" title="John Howe (illustrator)">John Howe</a> joined the project. Most of the imagery in the films is based on their various illustrations.<sup id="cite_ref-Lord_of_the_Films_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lord_of_the_Films-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Production_designer" title="Production designer">Production designer</a> <a href="/wiki/Grant_Major" title="Grant Major">Grant Major</a> was charged with the task of converting Lee and Howe's designs into architecture, creating models of the sets, while <a href="/wiki/Dan_Hennah" title="Dan Hennah">Dan Hennah</a> worked as <a href="/wiki/Art_director#In_film" title="Art director">art director</a>, scouting locations and organising the building of sets.
</p><p>Jackson's vision of <a href="/wiki/Middle-earth" title="Middle-earth">Middle-earth</a> was described as being "<a href="/wiki/Ray_Harryhausen" title="Ray Harryhausen">Ray Harryhausen</a> meets <a href="/wiki/David_Lean" title="David Lean">David Lean</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Randy_Cook" class="mw-redirect" title="Randy Cook">Randy Cook</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ROTK_SEE_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ROTK_SEE-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> Jackson wanted a gritty realism and historical regard for the fantasy, and attempted to make the world rational and believable. For example, the <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand_Army" title="New Zealand Army">New Zealand Army</a> helped build <a href="/wiki/Hobbiton" class="mw-redirect" title="Hobbiton">Hobbiton</a> months before filming began so the plants could really grow.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> Creatures were designed to be biologically believable, such as the enormous wings of the <a href="/wiki/Fell_beast_(Middle-earth)" class="mw-redirect" title="Fell beast (Middle-earth)">fell beast</a> to help it fly.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> In total, 48,000 pieces of armour, 500 bows, and 10,000 arrows were created by Weta Workshop.<sup id="cite_ref-Trilogy_book_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Trilogy_book-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> They also created many prosthetics, such as 1,800 pairs of Hobbit feet for the lead actors,<sup id="cite_ref-FOTR_SEE_15-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOTR_SEE-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> as well as many ears, noses, and heads for the cast, and around 19,000 costumes were woven and aged.<sup id="cite_ref-FOTR_SEE_15-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOTR_SEE-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> Every prop was specially designed by the Art Department, taking the different scales into account.<sup id="cite_ref-FOTR_SEE_15-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOTR_SEE-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Filming">Filming</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Lord_of_the_Rings_(film_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Filming">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Principal_photography_of_The_Lord_of_the_Rings_film_series" title="Principal photography of The Lord of the Rings film series">Principal photography of The Lord of the Rings film series</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Principal_photography" title="Principal photography">Principal photography</a> for all three films was conducted concurrently in many locations within New Zealand's conservation areas and national parks. Filming took place between 11 October 1999 and 22 December 2000, a period of 438 days. <a href="/wiki/Pick-up_(filmmaking)" title="Pick-up (filmmaking)">Pick-up</a> shoots were conducted annually from 2001 to 2003. The series was shot at over 150 different locations,<sup id="cite_ref-Trilogy_book_27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Trilogy_book-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> with seven different units shooting, as well as soundstages around <a href="/wiki/Wellington" title="Wellington">Wellington</a> and <a href="/wiki/Queenstown,_New_Zealand" title="Queenstown, New Zealand">Queenstown</a>. Along with Jackson directing the whole production, other unit directors included John Mahaffie, <a href="/wiki/Geoff_Murphy" title="Geoff Murphy">Geoff Murphy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fran_Walsh" title="Fran Walsh">Fran Walsh</a>, Barrie Osbourne, Rick Porras, and any other assistant director, producer, or writer available. Jackson monitored these units with live satellite feeds, and with the added pressure of constant script re-writes and the multiple units interpreting his envisioned result, he only got around four hours of sleep a night.<sup id="cite_ref-TTT_SEE_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TTT_SEE-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> Due to the remoteness of some of the locations, the crew would also bring survival kits in case helicopters could not reach the location to bring them home in time.<sup id="cite_ref-FOTR_SEE_15-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOTR_SEE-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand_Department_of_Conservation" class="mw-redirect" title="New Zealand Department of Conservation">New Zealand Department of Conservation</a> was criticised for approving the filming within national parks without adequate consideration of the adverse environmental effects and without public notification.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> The adverse effects of filming battle scenes in <a href="/wiki/Tongariro_National_Park" title="Tongariro National Park">Tongariro National Park</a> meant that the park later required restoration work.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Cast">Cast</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Lord_of_the_Rings_(film_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Cast">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Middle-earth_in_film#Cast" title="Middle-earth in film">Middle-earth in film §&#160;Cast</a></div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-production">Post-production</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Lord_of_the_Rings_(film_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Post-production">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Armadura_%C3%A9lfica.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Armadura_%C3%A9lfica.jpg/200px-Armadura_%C3%A9lfica.jpg" width="200" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Armadura_%C3%A9lfica.jpg/300px-Armadura_%C3%A9lfica.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Armadura_%C3%A9lfica.jpg/400px-Armadura_%C3%A9lfica.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Armadura_%C3%A9lfica.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An example of Elvish armour from the films.</div></div></div>
<p>Each film had the benefit of a full year of post-production time before its respective December release, often finishing in October–November, with the crew immediately going to work on the next film. In this period's later part, Jackson would move to London to supervise the scoring and continue editing, while having a computer feed for discussions to The Dorchester Hotel, and a "fat pipe" of Internet connections from <a href="/wiki/Pinewood_Studios" title="Pinewood Studios">Pinewood Studios</a> to look at the special effects. He had a video link and <a href="/wiki/5.1_surround_sound" title="5.1 surround sound">5.1 surround sound</a> to organise meetings, and listen to new music and sound effects generally wherever he was. The extended editions also had a tight schedule at the start of each year to complete special effects and music.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Editing">Editing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Lord_of_the_Rings_(film_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Editing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>To avoid pressure, Jackson hired a different editor for each film. <a href="/wiki/John_Gilbert_(film_editor)" title="John Gilbert (film editor)">John Gilbert</a> worked on the first film, <a href="/wiki/Michael_J._Horton" title="Michael J. Horton">Mike Horton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jabez_Olssen" title="Jabez Olssen">Jabez Olssen</a> on the second and longtime Jackson collaborator <a href="/wiki/Jamie_Selkirk" title="Jamie Selkirk">Jamie Selkirk</a> and <a href="/wiki/Annie_Collins" title="Annie Collins">Annie Collins</a> on the third. Daily rushes would often last up to four hours, with scenes being done throughout 1999–2002 for the rough (4½ hours) assemblies of the films.<sup id="cite_ref-FOTR_SEE_15-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOTR_SEE-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> In total, 1828&#160;km (six million feet) of film<sup id="cite_ref-Trilogy_book_27-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Trilogy_book-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> was edited down to the 11 hours and 23&#160;minutes (683&#160;minutes) of Extended running time. This was the final area of shaping of the films, when Jackson realised that sometimes the best scripting could be redundant on screen, as he picked apart scenes every day from multiple takes.
</p><p>The first film's editing was relatively easygoing, with Jackson coming up with the concept of an Extended Edition later on, although after a screening to New Line they had to re-edit the beginning for a prologue. <i>The Two Towers</i> was always acknowledged by the crew as the most difficult film to make, as "it had no beginning or end", and had the additional problem of inter-cutting storylines appropriately. Jackson even continued editing the film when that part of the schedule officially ended, resulting in some scenes, including the reforging of <a href="/wiki/And%C3%BAril" class="mw-redirect" title="Andúril">Andúril</a>, Gollum's back-story, and Saruman's demise, being moved to <i>The Return of the King</i>. Later, Saruman's demise was cut from the theatrical edition (but included in the Extended edition) when Jackson felt it was not starting the third film effectively enough.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> As with all parts of the third film's post-production, editing was very chaotic. The first time Jackson actually saw the completed film was at the Wellington premiere.
</p><p>Many filmed scenes remain unused, even in the Extended Editions. Promotional material for <i>The Fellowship of the Ring</i> contained an attack by <a href="/wiki/Orc_(Middle-earth)" title="Orc (Middle-earth)">Orcs</a> from Moria on Lothlórien after the Fellowship leaves Moria, replaced with a more suspenseful entrance for the Fellowship. Also cut were scenes from the book, including Frodo seeing more of Middle-earth at <a href="/wiki/Parth_Galen" class="mw-redirect" title="Parth Galen">Parth Galen</a> and an extended Council of Elrond,<sup id="cite_ref-FOTR_SEE_15-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOTR_SEE-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> and new scenes with an attack upon Frodo and Sam at the river <a href="/wiki/Anduin" title="Anduin">Anduin</a> by an Uruk-hai.<sup id="cite_ref-FOTR_SEE_15-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOTR_SEE-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> The major cut to <i>The Two Towers</i> featured Arwen and Elrond visiting Galadriel at Lothlórien, with Arwen then leading the Elven reinforcements to Helm's Deep.<sup id="cite_ref-TTT_SEE_19-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TTT_SEE-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> This scene, and a flashback to Arwen and Aragorn's first meeting, was cut during a revision of the film's plot; the Elves' appearance was explained with a telepathic communication between Elrond and Galadriel.<sup id="cite_ref-TTT_SEE_19-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TTT_SEE-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Éowyn was to have a greater role in defending the refugees in the <a href="/wiki/Glittering_Caves" class="mw-redirect" title="Glittering Caves">Glittering Caves</a> from Uruk-hai intruders,<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> while in Osgiliath, Faramir was to have a vision of Frodo becoming like Gollum,<sup id="cite_ref-TTT_SEE_19-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TTT_SEE-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> with Frodo and Sam having an extended fight sequence.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> Filmed for <i>The Return of the King</i> were two scenes present in the book; Sam using the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Middle-earth_objects#Phial_of_Galadriel" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Middle-earth objects">Phial of Galadriel</a> to pass the Watchers at <a href="/wiki/Cirith_Ungol" class="mw-redirect" title="Cirith Ungol">Cirith Ungol</a>, and further epilogue footage, with endings for Legolas and Gimli, Éowyn and Faramir's wedding and Aragorn's death and funeral.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> Sauron was to fight Aragorn at the Black Gate, but with Jackson deciding the scene was inappropriate, a computer-generated Troll was used instead.<sup id="cite_ref-ROTK_SEE_24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ROTK_SEE-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> To give context for Wormtongue killing Saruman, and Legolas in turn killing Wormtongue, it was to be revealed Wormtongue poisoned <a href="/wiki/Th%C3%A9odred" title="Théodred">Théodred</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> The final scene cut was Aragorn having his armour fitted for the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Morannon" title="Battle of the Morannon">Battle of the Black Gate</a> by the trilogy's armourers, which was the final scene filmed during principal photography.<sup id="cite_ref-ROTK_SEE_24-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ROTK_SEE-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> Peter Jackson has stated that he would like to include some of these unused scenes in a future "Ultimate Edition" home video release, also including out-takes.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Lord_of_the_Rings_(film_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_The_Lord_of_the_Rings_film_series" title="Music of The Lord of the Rings film series">Music of The Lord of the Rings film series</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Howard_Shore,_Canadian_Film_Centre,_2013-1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Howard_Shore%2C_Canadian_Film_Centre%2C_2013-1.jpg/220px-Howard_Shore%2C_Canadian_Film_Centre%2C_2013-1.jpg" width="220" height="314" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Howard_Shore%2C_Canadian_Film_Centre%2C_2013-1.jpg/330px-Howard_Shore%2C_Canadian_Film_Centre%2C_2013-1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Howard_Shore%2C_Canadian_Film_Centre%2C_2013-1.jpg/440px-Howard_Shore%2C_Canadian_Film_Centre%2C_2013-1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2100" data-file-height="3000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Howard_Shore,_Canadian_Film_Centre,_2013-1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Howard Shore composed, orchestrated, conducted, and produced the trilogy's music.</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Howard_Shore" title="Howard Shore">Howard Shore</a> composed, orchestrated, conducted, and produced the trilogy's music. He was hired in August 2000<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> and visited the set, and watched the assembly cuts of <i>The Fellowship of the Ring</i> and <i>The Return of the King</i>. In the music, Shore included many (85 to 110) <a href="/wiki/Leitmotifs" class="mw-redirect" title="Leitmotifs">leitmotifs</a> to represent various characters, cultures, and places - the largest catalogue of leitmotives in the history of cinema, surpassing - for comparison - that of the entire <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Star_Wars" title="Music of Star Wars">Star Wars saga</a>. For example, there are multiple leitmotifs just for the hobbits and the <a href="/wiki/Shire_(Middle-earth)" title="Shire (Middle-earth)">Shire</a>. Although the first film had some of its score recorded in Wellington,<sup id="cite_ref-FOTR_SEE_15-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOTR_SEE-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> virtually all of the trilogy's score was recorded in <a href="/wiki/Watford_Colosseum" class="mw-redirect" title="Watford Colosseum">Watford Town Hall</a> and mixed at <a href="/wiki/Abbey_Road_Studios" title="Abbey Road Studios">Abbey Road Studios</a>. Jackson planned to advise the score for six weeks each year in London, though for <i>The Two Towers</i> he stayed for twelve. As a <a href="/wiki/The_Beatles" title="The Beatles">Beatles</a> fan, Jackson had a photo tribute done there on the <a href="/wiki/Zebra_crossing" title="Zebra crossing">zebra crossing</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-TTT_SEE_19-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TTT_SEE-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The score is primarily played by the <a href="/wiki/London_Philharmonic_Orchestra" title="London Philharmonic Orchestra">London Philharmonic Orchestra</a> (ranging from 93 to 120 players throughout the recording), <a href="/wiki/London_Voices" title="London Voices">London Voices</a>, London Oratory School Schola boy choir, and many artists such as <a href="/w/index.php?title=Ben_Del_Maestro&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Ben Del Maestro (page does not exist)">Ben Del Maestro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Enya" title="Enya">Enya</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ren%C3%A9e_Fleming" title="Renée Fleming">Renée Fleming</a>, <a href="/wiki/James_Galway" title="James Galway">James Galway</a>, <a href="/wiki/Annie_Lennox" title="Annie Lennox">Annie Lennox</a> and <a href="/wiki/Emil%C3%ADana_Torrini" title="Emilíana Torrini">Emilíana Torrini</a> contributed. Even actors <a href="/wiki/Billy_Boyd_(actor)" title="Billy Boyd (actor)">Billy Boyd</a>, <a href="/wiki/Viggo_Mortensen" title="Viggo Mortensen">Viggo Mortensen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Liv_Tyler" title="Liv Tyler">Liv Tyler</a>, <a href="/wiki/Miranda_Otto" title="Miranda Otto">Miranda Otto</a> (extended cuts only for the latter two), and Peter Jackson (for a single gong sound in the second film) contributed to the score. Fran Walsh and Philippa Boyens served as librettists, writing lyrics to various music and songs, which <a href="/wiki/David_Salo" title="David Salo">David Salo</a> translated into Tolkien's languages. The third film's end song, "<a href="/wiki/Into_the_West_(song)" title="Into the West (song)">Into the West</a>", was a tribute to a young filmmaker Jackson and Walsh befriended named <a href="/wiki/Cameron_Duncan" title="Cameron Duncan">Cameron Duncan</a>, who died of cancer in 2003.<sup id="cite_ref-ROTK_SEE_24-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ROTK_SEE-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Shore composed a main theme for <i>The Fellowship</i> rather than many different character themes, and its strength and weaknesses in volume are depicted at different points in the series. On top of that, individual themes were composed to represent different cultures. Infamously, the amount of music Shore had to write every day for the third film increased dramatically to around seven minutes.<sup id="cite_ref-ROTK_SEE_24-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ROTK_SEE-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> The music for the series turned out to be a success and has been voted best movie soundtrack of all time for the six years running, passing <i><a href="/wiki/Schindler%27s_List" title="Schindler&#39;s List">Schindler's List</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Gladiator_(2000_film)" title="Gladiator (2000 film)">Gladiator</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Wars_(film)" title="Star Wars (film)">Star Wars</a></i> (1977), and <i><a href="/wiki/Out_of_Africa_(film)" title="Out of Africa (film)">Out of Africa</a></i> respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sound">Sound</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Lord_of_the_Rings_(film_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Sound">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Sound technicians spent the early part of the year trying to find the right sounds. Some, such as animal sounds like those of tigers and walruses, were bought. Human voices were also used. Fran Walsh contributed to the Nazgûl scream and David Farmer the <a href="/wiki/Warg_(Middle-earth)" class="mw-redirect" title="Warg (Middle-earth)">Warg</a> howls. Other sounds were unexpected: the fell beast's screech is taken from that of a donkey, and the <i><a href="/wiki/M%C3%BBmakil" class="mw-redirect" title="Mûmakil">mûmakil</a>'</i>s bellow comes from the beginning and end of a lion's roar. In addition, <a href="/wiki/Dubbing_(filmmaking)" title="Dubbing (filmmaking)">ADR</a> was used for most of the dialogue.
</p><p>The technicians worked with New Zealand locals to get many of the sounds. They re-recorded sounds in abandoned tunnels for an echo-like effect in the <a href="/wiki/Moria_(Middle-earth)" title="Moria (Middle-earth)">Moria</a> sequence. 20,000 New Zealand cricket fans provided the sound of the Uruk-hai army in <i>The Two Towers</i>, with Jackson acting as conductor during the innings break of a one-day international cricket match between England and New Zealand at <a href="/wiki/Westpac_Stadium" class="mw-redirect" title="Westpac Stadium">Westpac Stadium</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-TTT_SEE_19-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TTT_SEE-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> They spent time recording sounds in a graveyard at night, and also had construction workers drop stone blocks for the sounds of boulders firing and landing in <i>The Return of the King</i>. Mixing took place between August and November at "The Film Mix", before Jackson commissioned the building of a new studio in 2003. The building, however, had not yet been fully completed when they started mixing for <i>The Return of the King</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-ROTK_SEE_24-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ROTK_SEE-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Special_effects">Special effects</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Lord_of_the_Rings_(film_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Special effects">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Special_effects_of_The_Lord_of_the_Rings_film_series" title="Special effects of The Lord of the Rings film series">Special effects of The Lord of the Rings film series</a></div>
<p>The first film has around 540 effect shots, the second 799, and the third 1,488 (2,730 in total). The total increases to 3,420 with the extended editions. 260 visual effect artists began work on the series, and the number doubled by <i>The Two Towers</i>. The crew, led by <a href="/wiki/Jim_Rygiel" title="Jim Rygiel">Jim Rygiel</a> and Randy Cook, worked long hours, often overnight, to produce special effects within a short space of time. Jackson's active imagination was a driving force. For example, several major shots of Helm's Deep were produced within the last six weeks of post-production of <i>The Two Towers</i>, and the same happened again within the last six weeks on <i>The Return of the King</i>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Releases">Releases</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Lord_of_the_Rings_(film_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Releases">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Theatrical">Theatrical</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Lord_of_the_Rings_(film_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Theatrical">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The trilogy's online promotional trailer was first released on 27 April 2000, and set a new record for download hits, registering 1.7&#160;million hits in the first 24 hours of its release.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> The trailer used a selection from the soundtrack for <i><a href="/wiki/Braveheart" title="Braveheart">Braveheart</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Shawshank_Redemption" title="The Shawshank Redemption">The Shawshank Redemption</a></i> among other cuts. In 2001, 24&#160;minutes of footage from the series, primarily the <a href="/wiki/Moria_(Middle-earth)" title="Moria (Middle-earth)">Moria</a> sequence, was shown at the <a href="/wiki/Cannes_Film_Festival" title="Cannes Film Festival">Cannes Film Festival</a>, and was very well received.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> The showing also included an area designed to look like <a href="/wiki/Middle-earth" title="Middle-earth">Middle-earth</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Trilogy_book_27-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Trilogy_book-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><i><a href="/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings:_The_Fellowship_of_the_Ring" title="The Lord of the Rings: The Fellowship of the Ring">The Fellowship of the Ring</a></i> was released 19 December 2001. It grossed $47&#160;million in its U.S. opening weekend and made around $871&#160;million worldwide. A preview of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings:_The_Two_Towers" title="The Lord of the Rings: The Two Towers">The Two Towers</a></i> was inserted just before the end credits near the end of the film's theatrical run.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> A promotional trailer was later released, containing music re-scored from the film <i><a href="/wiki/Requiem_for_a_Dream" title="Requiem for a Dream">Requiem for a Dream</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> <i>The Two Towers</i> was released 18 December 2002. It grossed $62&#160;million in its first U.S. weekend and out-grossed its predecessor with $926&#160;million worldwide. The promotional trailer for <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings:_The_Return_of_the_King" title="The Lord of the Rings: The Return of the King">The Return of the King</a></i> was debuted exclusively before the New Line Cinema film <i><a href="/wiki/Secondhand_Lions" title="Secondhand Lions">Secondhand Lions</a></i> on 23 September 2003.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> Released 17 December 2003, its first U.S. weekend gross was $72&#160;million, and became the second film (after <i><a href="/wiki/Titanic_(1997_film)" title="Titanic (1997 film)">Titanic</a></i>) to gross over $1&#160;billion worldwide.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Home_media">Home media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Lord_of_the_Rings_(film_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Home media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The first two films were released on standard two-disc edition DVDs containing previews of the next film. The success of the theatrical cuts brought about four-disc Extended Editions, with new editing, added special effects and music.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> The extended cuts of the films and the included special features were spread over two discs, and a limited collector's edition was also released. <i>The Fellowship of the Ring</i> was released on 12 November 2002, containing 30&#160;minutes more footage, an Alan Lee painting of the Fellowship entering Moria, and the Moria Gate on the back of the sleeve; an <a href="/wiki/Argonath" class="mw-redirect" title="Argonath">Argonath</a>-styled bookend was included with the Collector's Edition. <i>The Two Towers</i>, released on 18 November 2003, contained 44&#160;minutes extra footage and a Lee painting of Gandalf the White's entrance; the Collector's Edition contained a Sméagol statue, with a crueller-looking statue of his Gollum persona available by order for a limited time.
</p><p><i>The Return of the King</i> was released on 14 December 2004, having 51&#160;minutes more footage, a Lee painting of the Grey Havens and a model of Minas Tirith for the Collector's Edition, with <a href="/wiki/Minas_Morgul" title="Minas Morgul">Minas Morgul</a> available by order for a limited time. The Special Extended DVD Editions also had in-sleeve maps of the Fellowship's travels. They have also played at cinemas, most notably for a 16 December 2003 marathon screening (dubbed "Trilogy Tuesday") culminating in a late afternoon screening of the third film. Attendees of "Trilogy Tuesday" were given a limited edition keepsake from <a href="/wiki/Sideshow_Collectibles" title="Sideshow Collectibles">Sideshow Collectibles</a> containing one random frame of film from each of the three movies. Both versions were put together in a Limited Edition "<a href="/wiki/Seamless_branching" title="Seamless branching">branching</a>" version, plus a new feature-length documentary by <a href="/w/index.php?title=Costa_Botes&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Costa Botes (page does not exist)">Costa Botes</a>. The complete series was released in a six-disc set on 14 November 2006.
</p><p>Warner Bros. released the trilogy's theatrical versions on <a href="/wiki/Blu-ray_Disc" class="mw-redirect" title="Blu-ray Disc">Blu-ray Disc</a> in a boxed set on 6 April 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> An extended edition Blu-ray box set was made available for pre-order from Amazon.com in March 2011 and was released on 28 June 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> Each film's extended Blu-ray version is identical to the extended DVD version; the total running time is longer due to added credit sequence listing the names of "<i>Lord of the Rings</i> fan-club members" who contributed to the project.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2014, brand new Blu-ray steelbook editions of the five-disc Extended Editions were released. The first, <i>The Fellowship of the Ring</i>, was released on 24 March 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> The discs are identical to those found in the previous five-disc Blu-ray set.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Reception">Reception</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Lord_of_the_Rings_(film_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Reception">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_and_critical_response">Public and critical response</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Lord_of_the_Rings_(film_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Public and critical response">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Unadjusted for inflation, <i>The Lord of the Rings</i> film series is the highest-grossing film trilogy worldwide of all time, higher even than other film franchises such as the <a href="/wiki/Star_Wars#Original_trilogy" title="Star Wars">original <i>Star Wars</i> trilogy</a> and <a href="/wiki/The_Godfather_(film_series)" title="The Godfather (film series)"><i>The Godfather</i> trilogy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> The film series grossed a total of $2.91 billion<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> and also tied a record with <i><a href="/wiki/Ben-Hur_(1959_film)" title="Ben-Hur (1959 film)">Ben-Hur</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Titanic_(1997_film)" title="Titanic (1997 film)">Titanic</a></i> for the total number of <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Academy Award">Academy Awards</a> won for a single film, with <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings:_The_Return_of_the_King" title="The Lord of the Rings: The Return of the King">The Return of the King</a></i> receiving eleven Oscars.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The majority of critics have also praised the series, with <a href="/wiki/Kenneth_Turan" title="Kenneth Turan">Kenneth Turan</a> of the <i><a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Times" title="Los Angeles Times">Los Angeles Times</a></i> writing that "the trilogy will not soon, if ever, find its equal".<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> Some were critical of the films' pacing and length: "It's a collection of spectacular set pieces without any sense of momentum driving them into one another" according to <i><a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Weekly" title="Philadelphia Weekly">Philadelphia Weekly</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On <a href="/wiki/Rotten_Tomatoes" title="Rotten Tomatoes">Rotten Tomatoes</a>, the films received approval ratings of 91%, 95%, and 93% respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-rotfel_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rotfel-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-rottower_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rottower-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-rotreturn_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rotreturn-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Metacritic" title="Metacritic">Metacritic</a>, based on its ratings for each film (92, 87, and 94 respectively),<sup id="cite_ref-metafel_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-metafel-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-metatower_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-metatower-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-metareturn_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-metareturn-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> features the series within the top ten of the best films of the decade.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> As of July 2016, every film is placed in the top 200 of Metacritic's 'Best Movies of all Time' list.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/CinemaScore" title="CinemaScore">CinemaScore</a> polls conducted during the opening weekend, cinema audiences gave the films an average grade of A-, A, and A+ respectively on an A+ to F scale.<sup id="cite_ref-cinemascore_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cinemascore-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The series appears in the <a href="/wiki/Dallas-Fort_Worth_Film_Critics_Association:_Top_10_Films" class="mw-redirect" title="Dallas-Fort Worth Film Critics Association: Top 10 Films">Dallas-Fort Worth Film Critics Association's Top 10 Films</a>, <i>Time</i> magazine's All-Time 100 Movies, and <a href="/wiki/James_Berardinelli" title="James Berardinelli">James Berardinelli</a>'s Top 100.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> In 2007, <i><a href="/wiki/USA_Today" title="USA Today">USA Today</a></i> named the series as the most important films of the past 25 years.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Entertainment_Weekly" title="Entertainment Weekly">Entertainment Weekly</a></i> put it on its end-of-the-decade, "best-of" list, saying, "Bringing a cherished book to the big screen? No sweat. Peter Jackson's trilogy — or, as we like to call it, our preciousssss — exerted its irresistible pull, on advanced Elvish speakers and neophytes alike."<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Paste_Magazine" class="mw-redirect" title="Paste Magazine">Paste Magazine</a></i> named it one of the 50 Best Movies of the Decade (2000–2009), ranking it at <abbr title="Number">No.</abbr> 4.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>
In another <i>Time</i> magazine list, the series ranks second in "Best Movies of the Decade".<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>
<i><a href="/wiki/Empire_(film_magazine)" title="Empire (film magazine)">Empire</a></i> magazine voted the films at #1 on the '32 Greatest Film Trilogies'.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> In addition, six characters and their respective actors made the list of 'The 100 Greatest Movie Characters', also compiled by <i>Empire</i>, with <a href="/wiki/Viggo_Mortensen" title="Viggo Mortensen">Viggo Mortensen</a>'s portrayal of Aragorn ranking No. 15, <a href="/wiki/Ian_McKellen" title="Ian McKellen">Ian McKellen</a>'s portrayal of Gandalf ranking No. 30, <a href="/wiki/Ian_Holm" title="Ian Holm">Ian Holm</a>'s portrayal of Bilbo Baggins (shared with <a href="/wiki/Martin_Freeman" title="Martin Freeman">Martin Freeman</a> for his portrayal of the same character in <i>The Hobbit</i> films) ranking No. 61, <a href="/wiki/Andy_Serkis" title="Andy Serkis">Andy Serkis</a>' portrayal of Gollum ranking No. 66, <a href="/wiki/Sean_Astin" title="Sean Astin">Sean Astin</a>'s portrayal of Samwise Gamgee ranking No. 77, and <a href="/wiki/Orlando_Bloom" title="Orlando Bloom">Orlando Bloom</a>'s portrayal of Legolas ranking No. 94.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Academy_Awards">Academy Awards</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Lord_of_the_Rings_(film_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Academy Awards">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_accolades_received_by_The_Lord_of_the_Rings_film_series" title="List of accolades received by The Lord of the Rings film series">List of accolades received by The Lord of the Rings film series</a></div>
<p>The three films together were nominated for a total of 30 <a href="/wiki/Academy_Awards" title="Academy Awards">Academy Awards</a>, of which they won 17, a record for any movie trilogy (the three nominations for <i><a href="/wiki/The_Hobbit:_An_Unexpected_Journey" title="The Hobbit: An Unexpected Journey">The Hobbit: An Unexpected Journey</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Hobbit:_The_Desolation_of_Smaug" title="The Hobbit: The Desolation of Smaug">The Hobbit: The Desolation of Smaug</a></i> along with the single nomination for <i><a href="/wiki/The_Hobbit:_The_Battle_of_the_Five_Armies" title="The Hobbit: The Battle of the Five Armies">The Hobbit: The Battle of the Five Armies</a></i> brings the series' total to 37 nominations). <i>The Fellowship of the Ring</i> earned thirteen nominations, the most of any film at the <a href="/wiki/74th_Academy_Awards" title="74th Academy Awards">74th Academy Awards</a>, winning four. <i>The Return of the King</i> won in every category in which it was nominated, setting the current Oscar record for the highest clean sweep, and its 11 <a href="/wiki/Academy_Awards" title="Academy Awards">Academy Awards</a> wins ties the record held by <i><a href="/wiki/Ben-Hur_(1959_film)" title="Ben-Hur (1959 film)">Ben-Hur</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Titanic_(1997_film)" title="Titanic (1997 film)">Titanic</a></i> (though both of those films had additional nominations that they ultimately lost). <i>The Return of the King</i> became only the second sequel to win the Oscar for Best Picture (after <i><a href="/wiki/The_Godfather_Part_II" title="The Godfather Part II">The Godfather Part II</a></i>) and the first fantasy film to receive this honor, though this has been widely perceived as an award by proxy for the entire series (the first two films were also nominated for Best Picture).<sup id="cite_ref-LA_Times_McNamara_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LA_Times_McNamara-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> No actors in any of the three films won Oscars, and <a href="/wiki/Ian_McKellen" title="Ian McKellen">Ian McKellen</a> was the only actor in the trilogy to receive a nomination, for his work in <i>The Fellowship of the Ring</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-LA_Times_McNamara_79-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LA_Times_McNamara-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li><i>The Fellowship of the Ring</i> – Nominations: 13, Wins: 4</li>
<li><i>The Two Towers</i> — Nominations: 6, Wins: 2</li>
<li><i>The Return of the King</i> — Nominations: 11, Wins: 11</li></ul>
<table class="wikitable" style="margin:left;">
