<p>As well as Academy Awards, each film in the series won the <a href="/wiki/Hugo_Award_for_Best_Dramatic_Presentation" title="Hugo Award for Best Dramatic Presentation">Hugo Award for Best Dramatic Presentation</a>, the <a href="/wiki/MTV_Movie_Award_for_Best_Movie" class="mw-redirect" title="MTV Movie Award for Best Movie">MTV Movie Award for Best Movie</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Saturn_Award_for_Best_Fantasy_Film" title="Saturn Award for Best Fantasy Film">Saturn Award for Best Fantasy Film</a>. The first and third films also won the <a href="/wiki/BAFTA_Award_for_Best_Film" title="BAFTA Award for Best Film">BAFTA Award for Best Film</a>. The soundtrack for <i>The Two Towers</i> did not receive a nomination because of a rule prohibiting a soundtrack including music from a previous soundtrack to be eligible for nomination. This rule was changed in time for <i>The Return of the King</i> to receive the Oscar for Best Music Score. The New York Film Critics Circle awarded <i>The Return of the King</i> its Best Picture Award at the 2003 Awards Ceremony, hosted by <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Johnston_(critic)" title="Andrew Johnston (critic)">Andrew Johnston</a>, chair of the organization at that time, who called it "a masterful piece of filmmaking."<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Reactions_to_changes_in_the_films_from_the_books">Reactions to changes in the films from the books</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Lord_of_the_Rings_(film_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Reactions to changes in the films from the books">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_original_characters_in_The_Lord_of_the_Rings_film_series" title="List of original characters in The Lord of the Rings film series">List of original characters in The Lord of the Rings film series</a></div>
<p>The film series provoked both positive and negative reaction from fans and scholars of the novels, and was sometimes seen as changing parts Tolkien felt thematically necessary in terms of characters, themes, events and subtlety. Some fans of the book who disagreed with such changes have released <a href="/wiki/Fan_edit" title="Fan edit">fan edits</a> of the films such as <i>The Lord of the Rings: The Purist Edition</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-cimmerian_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cimmerian-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> which removed many of the changes to bring them closer to the original.
</p><p>Various changes to characters such as <a href="/wiki/Gandalf" title="Gandalf">Gandalf</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aragorn" title="Aragorn">Aragorn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arwen" title="Arwen">Arwen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Denethor" title="Denethor">Denethor</a>, <a href="/wiki/Faramir" title="Faramir">Faramir</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gimli_(Middle-earth)" title="Gimli (Middle-earth)">Gimli</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Frodo_Baggins" title="Frodo Baggins">Frodo</a>, when considered together, were seen by some to alter the tone and themes found in the books. Several critics contend that the portrayal of women, especially Arwen, in the films is thematically faithful to (or compatible with) Tolkien's writings despite some differences.<sup id="cite_ref-akers-jordan_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-akers-jordan-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-chance_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chance-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-gaydosik_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gaydosik-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-thum_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thum-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup>
<a href="/wiki/Wayne_G._Hammond" title="Wayne G. Hammond">Wayne G. Hammond</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Tolkien_research" title="Tolkien research">Tolkien scholar</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> said of the first two films that he found them to be "travesties as adaptations... faithful only on a basic level of plot" and that many characters had not been depicted faithfully to their appearance in the novel.<sup id="cite_ref-croft_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-croft-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-kirst_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kirst-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> Other critics have argued that Tolkien's characters were weakened and misinterpreted by their portrayal in the films.<sup id="cite_ref-revolutionSF_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-revolutionSF-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-timmons_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-timmons-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Wiggins_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wiggins-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Changes to events (such as the Elves participating at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Hornburg" title="Battle of the Hornburg">Battle of Helm's Deep</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> Faramir taking the hobbits to <a href="/wiki/Osgiliath" class="mw-redirect" title="Osgiliath">Osgiliath</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-forum.barrowdowns.com_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-forum.barrowdowns.com-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> and the deletion of the chapter "<a href="/wiki/The_Scouring_of_the_Shire" title="The Scouring of the Shire">The Scouring of the Shire</a>") are also seen as changing Tolkien's themes.<sup id="cite_ref-forum.barrowdowns.com_95-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-forum.barrowdowns.com-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Janet_Brennan_Croft" title="Janet Brennan Croft">Janet Brennan Croft</a> criticized the films using Tolkien's own terms "anticipation" and "flattening", which she used in critiquing a <a href="/wiki/Adaptations_of_The_Lord_of_the_Rings#Early_efforts" title="Adaptations of The Lord of the Rings">proposed film script</a>. She contrasts Tolkien's subtlety with Jackson's tendency to show "too much too soon".<sup id="cite_ref-Croft2_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Croft2-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Supporters of the series assert that it is a worthy interpretation of the book and that most of the changes were necessary.<sup id="cite_ref-Lord_of_the_Films_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lord_of_the_Films-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> Many who worked on the series are fans of the book, including <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Lee" title="Christopher Lee">Christopher Lee</a>, who (alone among the cast) had actually met Tolkien in person,<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Philippa_Boyens" title="Philippa Boyens">Boyens</a> once noted that no matter what, it is simply their interpretation of the book. Jackson once said that to simply summarize the story on screen would be a mess, and in his own words, "Sure, it's not really <i>The Lord of the Rings</i>... but it could still be a pretty damn cool movie."<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> Other fans also claim that, despite any changes, the films serve as a tribute to the book, appealing to those who have not yet read it, and even leading some to do so. The Movie Guide for The Encyclopedia of <a href="/wiki/Arda_(Middle-earth)" class="mw-redirect" title="Arda (Middle-earth)">Arda</a> (an online Tolkien encyclopedia) states that Jackson's films were exceptional since filming the whole story of <i>The Lord of the Rings</i> was probably impossible.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> This notion is partially supported by a review published in 2005 that otherwise criticized a lack of "faithfulness to Tolkien's spirit and tone."<sup id="cite_ref-bratman_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bratman-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup>
<a href="/wiki/Douglas_Kellner" title="Douglas Kellner">Douglas Kellner</a> argues that the conservative community spirit of Tolkien's Shire is reflected in Jackson's films as well as the division of the Fellowship into "squabbling races".<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> In a 2006 review, film theorist Kristin Thompson was critical about the fact that film studies were undertaken by literary researchers and about the frequent denigration of Jackson's work in the collected essays.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Legacy">Legacy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Lord_of_the_Rings_(film_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Legacy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="quotebox pullquote floatright" style="width:376px;&#32;;"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303512">.mw-parser-output .quotebox{background-color:#F9F9F9;border:1px solid #aaa;box-sizing:border-box;padding:10px;font-size:88%}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatleft{margin:0.5em 1.4em 0.8em 0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatright{margin:0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.centered{margin:0.5em auto 0.8em auto}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatleft p,.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatright p{font-style:inherit}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-title{background-color:#F9F9F9;text-align:center;font-size:larger;font-weight:bold}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote.quoted:before{font-family:"Times New Roman",serif;font-weight:bold;font-size:large;color:gray;content:" “ ";vertical-align:-45%;line-height:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote.quoted:after{font-family:"Times New Roman",serif;font-weight:bold;font-size:large;color:gray;content:" ” ";line-height:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .left-aligned{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .right-aligned{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .center-aligned{text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .quotebox cite{display:block;font-style:normal}@media screen and (max-width:360px){.mw-parser-output .quotebox{min-width:100%;margin:0 0 0.8em!important;float:none!important}}</style>
<div class="quotebox-quote quoted left-aligned" style="">They eviscerated the book by making it an action movie for young people aged 15 to 25, and it seems that <i><a href="/wiki/The_Hobbit_(film_series)" title="The Hobbit (film series)">The Hobbit</a></i> will be the same kind of film. [...] Tolkien has become a monster, devoured by his own popularity and absorbed by the absurdity of our time. The chasm between the beauty and seriousness of the work, and what it has become, has gone too far for me. Such commercialisation has reduced the aesthetic and philosophical impact of this creation to nothing. There is only one solution for me: turning my head away.</div>
<p><cite class="right-aligned" style="">—<a href="/wiki/Christopher_Tolkien" title="Christopher Tolkien">Christopher Tolkien</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Le_Monde" title="Le Monde">Le Monde</a>,</i> 9 July 2012<sup id="cite_ref-Le_Monde_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Le_Monde-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup></cite>
</p>
</div>
<p>The release of the films saw a surge of interest in <i>The Lord of the Rings</i> and Tolkien's other works, vastly increasing his impact on popular culture.<sup id="cite_ref-surge_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-surge-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> The success of the films spawned numerous video games and many other kinds of merchandise.
</p><p>It was rumored that the Tolkien family became split on the series, with <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Tolkien" title="Christopher Tolkien">Christopher Tolkien</a> and his son <a href="/wiki/Simon_Tolkien" title="Simon Tolkien">Simon Tolkien</a> feuding over whether or not it was a good idea to adapt.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> Christopher has since denied these claims, saying, "My own position is that <i>The Lord of the Rings</i> is peculiarly unsuitable to transformation into visual dramatic form. The suggestions that have been made that I 'disapprove' of the films, even to the extent of thinking ill of those with whom I may differ, are wholly without foundation." He added that he had never "expressed any such feeling".<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> In 2012, however, he described the films as having "eviscerated" the book, and criticized the resulting "commercialisation" of his father's work.<sup id="cite_ref-Le_Monde_104-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Le_Monde-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Effects_on_the_film_industry_and_tourism">Effects on the film industry and tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Lord_of_the_Rings_(film_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Effects on the film industry and tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>As a result of the series' success, Peter Jackson has become a major player in the film business (sometimes called a <a href="/wiki/Business_magnate" title="Business magnate">mogul</a>) in the mold of <a href="/wiki/Steven_Spielberg" title="Steven Spielberg">Steven Spielberg</a> and <a href="/wiki/George_Lucas" title="George Lucas">George Lucas</a>, in the process befriending some industry heavyweights like <a href="/wiki/Bryan_Singer" title="Bryan Singer">Bryan Singer</a> and <a href="/wiki/Frank_Darabont" title="Frank Darabont">Frank Darabont</a>. Jackson has since founded his own film production company, <a href="/wiki/Wingnut_Films" class="mw-redirect" title="Wingnut Films">Wingnut Films</a>, as well as Wingnut Interactive, a video game company. He was also finally given a chance to remake <i><a href="/wiki/King_Kong_(2005_film)" title="King Kong (2005 film)">King Kong</a></i> in 2005. The film was a critical and box office success, although not as successful as <i>The Lord of the Rings</i> series. Jackson has been called a "favourite son" of New Zealand.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> In 2004, Howard Shore toured with <i>The Lord of the Rings Symphony</i>, playing two hours of the score. Along with the <a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_(film_series)" title="Harry Potter (film series)"><i>Harry Potter</i> films</a>, the series has renewed interest in the fantasy film genre. <a href="/wiki/Tourism_for_New_Zealand" class="mw-redirect" title="Tourism for New Zealand">Tourism for New Zealand</a> is up, possibly due to its exposure in the series,<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> with the country's tourism industry waking up to an audience's familiarity.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Air_New_Zealand_Airbus_A320_Lord_of_the_Rings_livery_Creek.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Air_New_Zealand_Airbus_A320_Lord_of_the_Rings_livery_Creek.jpg/300px-Air_New_Zealand_Airbus_A320_Lord_of_the_Rings_livery_Creek.jpg" width="300" height="195" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Air_New_Zealand_Airbus_A320_Lord_of_the_Rings_livery_Creek.jpg/450px-Air_New_Zealand_Airbus_A320_Lord_of_the_Rings_livery_Creek.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Air_New_Zealand_Airbus_A320_Lord_of_the_Rings_livery_Creek.jpg/600px-Air_New_Zealand_Airbus_A320_Lord_of_the_Rings_livery_Creek.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="664" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Air_New_Zealand_Airbus_A320_Lord_of_the_Rings_livery_Creek.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Air_New_Zealand" title="Air New Zealand">Air New Zealand</a> painted this <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A320_family" title="Airbus A320 family">Airbus A320</a> in <i>The Lord of the Rings</i> livery to help promote the films.</div></div></div>
<p>In December 2002, <a href="/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings_Motion_Picture_Trilogy:_The_Exhibition" title="The Lord of the Rings Motion Picture Trilogy: The Exhibition">The Lord of the Rings Motion Picture Trilogy: The Exhibition</a> opened at the <a href="/wiki/Museum_of_New_Zealand_Te_Papa_Tongarewa" title="Museum of New Zealand Te Papa Tongarewa">Te Papa museum</a> in <a href="/wiki/Wellington" title="Wellington">Wellington</a>, New Zealand. As of 2007, the exhibition has traveled to seven other cities around the world. A <a href="/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings_(theatre)#Toronto" class="mw-redirect" title="The Lord of the Rings (theatre)">musical adaptation</a> of the book was launched in <a href="/wiki/Toronto" title="Toronto">Toronto</a>, Ontario, Canada, in 2006, but it closed after mostly poor reviews. A <a href="/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings_(theatre)#London" class="mw-redirect" title="The Lord of the Rings (theatre)">shortened version</a> opened in London, United Kingdom, in the summer of 2007. 
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Legal_disputes">Legal disputes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Lord_of_the_Rings_(film_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Legal disputes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The legacy of <i>The Lord of the Rings</i> is also that of court cases over profits from the trilogy. Sixteen cast members (<a href="/w/index.php?title=Noel_Appleby&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Noel Appleby (page does not exist)">Noel Appleby</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">&#160;(<a href="https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/Noel_Appleby" class="extiw" title="de:Noel Appleby">de</a>)</span>, <a href="/wiki/Jed_Brophy" title="Jed Brophy">Jed Brophy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mark_Ferguson" title="Mark Ferguson">Mark Ferguson</a>, Ray Henwood, <a href="/wiki/Bruce_Hopkins_(actor)" title="Bruce Hopkins (actor)">Bruce Hopkins</a>, William Johnson, <a href="/wiki/Nathaniel_Lees" title="Nathaniel Lees">Nathaniel Lees</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sarah_McLeod" title="Sarah McLeod">Sarah McLeod</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ian_Mune" title="Ian Mune">Ian Mune</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paul_Norell" title="Paul Norell">Paul Norell</a>, <a href="/wiki/Craig_Parker" title="Craig Parker">Craig Parker</a>, <a href="/wiki/Robert_Pollock_(New_Zealand_actor)" class="mw-redirect" title="Robert Pollock (New Zealand actor)">Robert Pollock</a>, <a href="/wiki/Martyn_Sanderson" title="Martyn Sanderson">Martyn Sanderson</a>, Peter Tait and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Stephan_Ure&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Stephan Ure (page does not exist)">Stephan Ure</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">&#160;(<a href="https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stephan_Ure" class="extiw" title="de:Stephan Ure">de</a>)</span>) sued over the lack of revenue from merchandise bearing their appearance. The case was resolved out of court in 2008. The settlement came too late for Appleby, who died of cancer in 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Saul_Zaentz" title="Saul Zaentz">Saul Zaentz</a> also filed a lawsuit in 2004 claiming he had not been paid all of his royalties. 
</p><p>The next year, Jackson himself sued the studio over profits from the first film, slowing development of the <i>Hobbit</i> prequels until late 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/The_Tolkien_Trust" title="The Tolkien Trust">The Tolkien Trust</a> filed a lawsuit in February 2008, for violating Tolkien's original deal over the rights that they would earn 7.5% of the gross from any films based on his works.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> The Trust sought compensation of $150&#160;million.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> A judge denied them this option, but allowed them to win compensation from the act of the studio ignoring the contract itself.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> On 8 September 2009, the dispute was settled.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Hobbit_prequel_trilogy"><i>The Hobbit</i> prequel trilogy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Lord_of_the_Rings_(film_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: The Hobbit prequel trilogy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/The_Hobbit_(film_series)" title="The Hobbit (film series)">The Hobbit (film series)</a></div>
<p>The success of the <i>Lord of the Rings</i> trilogy led to Jackson directing a trilogy of prequels based on Tolkien's children's book <i><a href="/wiki/The_Hobbit" title="The Hobbit">The Hobbit</a></i>. The films, which were released between 2012 and 2014, used much of the cast and crew of <i>The Lord of the Rings</i>, including <a href="/wiki/Ian_McKellen" title="Ian McKellen">Ian McKellen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Andy_Serkis" title="Andy Serkis">Andy Serkis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hugo_Weaving" title="Hugo Weaving">Hugo Weaving</a>, <a href="/wiki/Elijah_Wood" title="Elijah Wood">Elijah Wood</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ian_Holm" title="Ian Holm">Ian Holm</a> (as older Bilbo), <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Lee" title="Christopher Lee">Christopher Lee</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cate_Blanchett" title="Cate Blanchett">Cate Blanchett</a> and <a href="/wiki/Orlando_Bloom" title="Orlando Bloom">Orlando Bloom</a> who reprised their roles. Although the <i>Hobbit</i> films were even more commercially successful than <i>The Lord of the Rings</i>, they received mixed reviews from critics.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Video_games">Video games</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Lord_of_the_Rings_(film_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Video games">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Numerous video games were released to supplement the film series. They include: <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings:_The_Two_Towers_(video_game)" title="The Lord of the Rings: The Two Towers (video game)">The Two Towers</a>,</i> <a href="/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings_(pinball)" title="The Lord of the Rings (pinball)">Pinball</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings:_The_Return_of_the_King_(video_game)" title="The Lord of the Rings: The Return of the King (video game)">The Return of the King</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings:_The_Third_Age" title="The Lord of the Rings: The Third Age">The Third Age</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings:_The_Third_Age_(GBA)" class="mw-redirect" title="The Lord of the Rings: The Third Age (GBA)"><i>The Third Age</i> (GBA)</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings:_Tactics" title="The Lord of the Rings: Tactics">Tactics</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings:_The_Battle_for_Middle-earth" title="The Lord of the Rings: The Battle for Middle-earth">The Battle for Middle-earth</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings:_The_Battle_for_Middle-earth_II" title="The Lord of the Rings: The Battle for Middle-earth II">The Battle for Middle-earth II</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings:_The_Battle_for_Middle-earth_II:_The_Rise_of_the_Witch-king" title="The Lord of the Rings: The Battle for Middle-earth II: The Rise of the Witch-king">The Battle for Middle-earth II: The Rise of the Witch-king</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings_Online" title="The Lord of the Rings Online">The Lord of the Rings Online</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings:_Conquest" title="The Lord of the Rings: Conquest">Conquest</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings:_Aragorn%27s_Quest" title="The Lord of the Rings: Aragorn&#39;s Quest">Aragorn's Quest</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings:_War_in_the_North" title="The Lord of the Rings: War in the North">War in the North</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Lego_The_Lord_of_the_Rings_(video_game)" title="Lego The Lord of the Rings (video game)">Lego The Lord of the Rings</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Guardians_of_Middle-earth" title="Guardians of Middle-earth">Guardians of Middle-earth</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Lego_The_Hobbit_(video_game)" title="Lego The Hobbit (video game)">Lego The Hobbit (video game)</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Middle-earth:_Shadow_of_Mordor" title="Middle-earth: Shadow of Mordor">Middle-earth: Shadow of Mordor</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Middle-earth:_Shadow_of_War" title="Middle-earth: Shadow of War">Middle-earth: Shadow of War</a></i>.
</p>

<li id="cite_note-Le_Monde-104"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-Le_Monde_104-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Le_Monde_104-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web">Rérolle, Raphaëlle (5 July 2012). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.lemonde.fr/culture/article/2012/07/05/tolkien-l-anneau-de-la-discorde_1729858_3246.html">"Tolkien, l'anneau de la discorde"</a>. <i>Le Monde</i><span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">4 August</span> 2012</span>. <q>Ils ont éviscéré le livre, en en faisant un film d'action pour les 15–25 ans. Et il paraît que <i>Le Hobbit</i> sera du même acabit. [...] Tolkien est devenu un monstre, dévoré par sa popularité et absorbé par l'absurdité de l'époque. Le fossé qui s'est creusé entre la beauté, le sérieux de l'œuvre, et ce qu'elle est devenue, tout cela me dépasse. Un tel degré de commercialisation réduit à rien la portée esthétique et philosophique de cette création. Il ne me reste qu'une seule solution&#160;: tourner la tête.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.jtitle=Le+Monde&amp;rft.atitle=Tolkien%2C+l%27anneau+de+la+discorde&amp;rft.date=2012-07-05&amp;rft.aulast=R%C3%A9rolle&amp;rft.aufirst=Rapha%C3%ABlle&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.lemonde.fr%2Fculture%2Farticle%2F2012%2F07%2F05%2Ftolkien-l-anneau-de-la-discorde_1729858_3246.html&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AThe+Lord+of+the+Rings+%28film+series%29" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/></span>
